Sino-British Joint Commission for the Demarcation of the Yunnan-Burma Border —Exchange of Notes Between the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the British Ambassador— Re-surveying the Old Border in the Southern Section of the Yunnan-Burma Border 98

Since the Ban Hong incident occurred last spring, the Chinese and British sides have had differing opinions. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs believes that the crux of the case lies in the undetermined boundary line in the southern section of the Yunnan-Burma border and has discussed the matter with the British Ambassador, forming a joint commission to re-survey the old border. After several discussions, two notes were exchanged on the 9th of this month. The original text was released yesterday (the 17th) as follows:

First Note from the British Ambassador (Translation)

"Regarding the undetermined boundary problem in the southern section of the Yunnan-Burma border referred to in Sections 3 and 4 of the Supplementary Convention to the Anglo-Chinese Convention Regarding Burma, signed in Beijing on February 4, 1897, the two parties have recently consulted on a solution. The Ambassador hereby declares that the British Government and the Indian Government accept the following terms of reference regarding the establishment and authority of the Border Commission mandated to investigate the said undetermined border section: (1) The Government of the Republic of China, on the one hand, and the Government of Great Britain and the Government of India, on the other hand, being now desirous of settling the long-pending question of the Yunnan-Burma border southern section and being motivated by a true spirit of compromise and mutual concession, hereby agree to establish a joint border commission composed of five members, with each side appointing two members, and with the Chairman of the Council of the League of Nations selecting one neutral member, who shall be the Chairman of the Commission. In the event that the opinions of other members differ and are equal in number, the chairman shall have the final vote. (2) The first responsibility of the Commission shall be to determine in the field the boundary line stipulated in Sections 3 and 4 of Article 3 of the 1897 Treaty relating to the undetermined border and to plot it on a map. When interpreting the text of the treaty that has not been given the same interpretation by the respective governments, the Commission shall give due consideration to the points stipulated and specified in the above-mentioned sections of the treaty, namely the intersections, watersheds, and place names contained in the text. (3) The second responsibility of the Commission shall be as follows: If any issues arise that they believe, based on mutual concession, should be subject to partial modification of the agreed boundary line, as specified in Article 6 of the original treaty, the Commission shall report to the respective governments for consideration based on their field inspections. (4) The Chinese and British members may, if they deem it necessary, provide their individual views for consideration by the respective governments. The Ambassador hereby requests Your Minister to confirm that the Government of the Republic of China also accepts the above-mentioned terms of reference. This note is hereby sent to Your Minister for review and response. Dated the 9th day of April, 1935."

First Reply Note from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs: "Regarding the reply, I acknowledge receipt of Your Excellency's note of today stating (repeating the original text of the note) and etc. With regard to the Border Commission mandated to investigate the undetermined border section in the southern section of the Yunnan-Burma border, the Minister hereby declares that the Government of the Republic of China also accepts the above-mentioned terms of reference regarding the establishment and authority of the Commission. This note is hereby sent to Your Excellency for review and response. Dated the ninth day of April in the twenty-fourth year of the Republic of China."

Second Note from the British Ambassador (Translation): "Regarding the establishment and authority of the Border Commission to investigate the undetermined border section in the southern section of the Yunnan-Burma border, as per the documents exchanged between our two parties today, the Ambassador hereby certifies, on behalf of the British Government and the Indian Government, that our respective governments have further understandings for negotiating a recommended solution for the said undetermined border section as follows: Based on the Commission's report, or based on geographical, historical, or political factors seemingly related to this issue, any future modification issues shall be discussed by both parties in a spirit of compromise and mutual concession. For the purpose of conducting these future negotiations, a conference shall be convened in Nanjing, if necessary, bringing together representatives from the respective governments, including representatives from Yunnan and Burma. The conclusions of the Commission's report and the results of any subsequent negotiations shall be stipulated in a new agreement. Prior to the signing of this new agreement, the respective governments shall each retain their original positions on this border section issue. The Ambassador hereby requests Your Minister, on behalf of the Government of the Republic of China, to certify the aforementioned additional understandings regarding this negotiation. This note is hereby sent to Your Minister for review and response. Dated the 9th day of April, 1935."

Second Reply Note from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs: "Regarding the reply, I acknowledge receipt of Your Excellency's note of today stating (repeating the original text of the note) and etc. The Minister hereby certifies the above-mentioned understanding on behalf of the Government of the Republic of China. This note is hereby sent to Your Excellency for review and response. Dated the ninth day of April in the twenty-fourth year of the Republic of China."

Birthday of the Revolutionary Pioneer, You Shaowan —Old Comrades of the Revive China Society Celebrate You's Birthday— A Preparatory Committee for Birthday Celebrations is Organized in Hong Kong 99

Guangzhou Correspondence: You Lie, courtesy name Shaowan, a revolutionary pioneer, is now 71 years old. He is a native of Shunde, Guangdong. In his early years, he traveled and engaged in revolutionary activities. Together with Sun Yat-sen, Yang Quyun, Yang Heling, Chen Shaobai, Lu Haodong, Cheng Yaozhen, Zheng Shiliang, and others, he founded the Revive China Society. Later, he founded the Revolutionary Alliance, with Sun Yat-sen as the president, and Mr. You presided over affairs in Southeast Asia. In the early days of the revolution, Sun, You, Yang (Heling), and Chen (Shaobai) were known as the "Four Great Bandits." After the founding of the Republic of China, You retired after his success and traveled to various countries in Europe and America. Recently, due to old age, he retired to Hong Kong, devoting himself to the study of Confucian classics and medical books. He has written books such as "Confucius's Theory of Revolution" and "Annotations to the Four Books." He also practices medicine in Hong Kong. Mr. You dedicated himself to the party and the country and did not have time to care for his family. His parents and wife passed away one after another long ago. Now he is all alone and living in extreme poverty. Xiao Focheng, Zou Lu, Li Xiangen, Zhong Rongguang, Song Juren, Li Jitang, Huang Mingtang, and others, believing that Mr. You is old and virtuous, and is the beacon of the revolutionary pioneers, have joined forces with the old comrades of the former Revive China Society and the members of the Revolutionary Memorial Society, as Mr. You is now celebrating his seventy-first birthday. They have specially organized the You Family Longevity Celebration Preparatory Committee in Hong Kong, and have designated the 29th of this month to celebrate Mr. You's birthday. Important figures from the party and the country, as well as Mr. You's relatives and friends, are all participating. Preparations have now begun, and notices have been sent out to solicit articles from various celebrities. Furthermore, Feng Ziyou, an old comrade of the Revolutionary Alliance, sent a congratulatory couplet to You, saying, "During the revival of the Han Dynasty, who remembers the fisherman Yan Chushi? At the Xiangshan Conference, we all worshiped Lord Guo Linggong on his lone ride."

Xiao Focheng Goes to Siam —The Siamese Government Increasingly Oppresses Overseas Chinese— 100

Shantou Correspondence: Xiao Focheng, Central Committee Member and Standing Committee Member of the Southwest Political Council, grew up in Siam and regards Siam almost as his hometown. Xiao, feeling that he is old and suffering from a cough, repeatedly wanted to return to Siam for recuperation last winter when it was cold, but he did not go because he was unwilling to leave his political career. Xiao has two sons. The elder son, Song Jian, is in Guangzhou serving him and also holding a position on the Power Commission. The younger son, Song Qin, is the supervisor of the Chao Hai Customs. Song Qin left Shantou for Guangzhou the day before yesterday. According to sources from the Customs Supervision Office, Xiao has booked two first-class cabins on the Taikoo Shipping Company's Jiangsu ship to Siam, accompanied by Song Jian. He is scheduled to arrive in Hong Kong on the 14th and can pass through Shantou on the 15th. He is expected to go directly to Siam from Shantou. Song Qin went to Guangzhou to see his father and brother off.

Approximately 60,000 overseas Chinese have returned to Shantou from Siam this spring. Among them are representatives of Siamese business groups. It is said that there are no less than 600,000 overseas Chinese residing in Bangkok. After the establishment of the new government, they consult with strong neighbors on everything and oppress overseas Chinese. They have increased ten types of taxes, such as goods tax, population tax, landing tax, residence tax, and pawnshop tax. They also intend to increase the landing tax again, from 150 baht per person to 200 baht. Income tax and inheritance tax are also being planned. They also forcibly implement assimilation education. Overseas Chinese girls, from the ages of seven to fourteen, must attend Siamese schools. Overseas Chinese teachers and curricula are greatly restricted. They are only allowed to study Chinese for one hour each day. Twenty-four overseas Chinese schools have been closed down. Since China and Siam have not signed a commercial treaty, the 1.5 million overseas Chinese in Siam are suffering from the unfair treatment of a country without a treaty. Siam's exports are mainly rice and timber. Its rice relies entirely on Hong Kong, Guangzhou, Shantou, and other places for sales. If the import of Siamese rice is banned, Siam's economy will be hit, which will surely prompt the Siamese government to come to its senses.

Minister Kong Comes to Shanghai 101

Kong Xiangxi left Beijing by night express train yesterday and arrived in Shanghai this morning.

Annual Meeting of Foreign Taxpayers

Passed a Motion to Postpone Telephone Rate Increase

Japanese Residents Vigorously Argued, Meeting Atmosphere Became Highly Agitated

A Special Committee Was Organized to Study and Handle It

Motions to Dismiss the Orchestra and Levy Taxes on Vacant Land Were Rejected

The annual meeting of foreign taxpayers in the Shanghai Public Concession was held yesterday afternoon at 5:00 PM at the Grand Theater on Jing'an Temple Road. A total of 897 people attended, with Japanese residents accounting for more than half. The meeting adjourned at approximately 8:00 PM. All eleven motions were discussed. During the final discussion, when Mr. Kanematsu and others from the Japanese residents proposed that the Board of Directors negotiate with the telephone company to postpone the rate increase, the atmosphere at the meeting became extremely tense. As a result, the motion to postpone the telephone rate increase was passed with amendments, and a special committee was organized to handle it. The details are recorded below:

Meeting Agenda

The meeting began at 5:00 PM sharp. Foreign taxpayers flocked to participate, with a total of 897 attendees, more than half of whom were Japanese residents. The agenda consisted of eleven items: (1) Election of the Chairman, Mr. Baker was elected; (2) Election of the Meeting Secretary, Mr. Beasley was elected; (3) Request the attendees to adopt the rules of procedure; (4) The Chairman of the Board to present the work report and accounts of the previous year for approval; (5) The Chairman of the Board to present the budget proposal for the current year for approval; (6) Election of one Real Estate Committee member, Mr. Peake was elected; (7) Election of four directors of the Public Hospital, Dr. Dunn, Dr. Barson, Mr. Caran, and Mr. Boulder were elected; (8) Mr. Hausenrobe's motion to transfer the orchestra to a private organization with an annual subsidy of 150,000 yuan; (9) Mr. Hausenrob's motion to investigate the possibility of levying taxes on vacant houses, vacant land, and unregistered land, and to publish the results; (10) Mr. Hausenlai's motion to raise 5 million yuan to purchase land and expand roads; (11) Mr. Kanematsu's motion to request the Board of Directors to negotiate with the telephone company to postpone the rate increase.

Chairman's Report

After passing the third item on the agenda, Chairman Arnold rose and gave a speech, reporting on the work and accounts of the previous year and requesting approval. Chairman Arnold first mentioned that the security situation in the past year was very good. He then stated that Shanghai, due to the impact of the global economic depression and China's economic difficulties, was facing a particularly serious unemployment problem. In the first three months of this year, no less than 34 factories in the Public Concession closed down, affecting approximately 20,000 workers. Therefore, maintaining security required redoubled attention.

Extramural Road Issues

The negotiation of extramural road issues began from July 1930 to June 1932. A draft resolution had already been prepared, but both the municipal government and the Board of Directors representatives had to seek instructions from their superiors. The proposed draft was a matter of principle and did not include specific measures. For the sake of prudence, the Bureau sought the opinions of the Consular Body on this matter. By August, the representatives of the United Kingdom and the United States had notified that their respective governments had expressed approval, but the Japanese Consul General did not agree. The main reason seemed to be the policing issue. After continued discussions from 1933 to the spring of 1934, an agreement was reached on the number and organization of police officers. As for the size of the district, in October, the Chinese representative proposed that a narrow strip of land be demarcated on each side of the roads, including several Bureau properties. The Japanese Consul General did not agree to this proposal and put forward a counter-proposal, which was not accepted by the Chinese side. Throughout the negotiation process, the representatives of the municipal government were extremely open and candid, and the various points that had been agreed upon seemed appropriate. As for the present situation, the negotiation seemed to have stalled, as the difficulties that arose were unexpected, and the final result was difficult to predict.

West District Electricity Issue

The extramural road issue involves various public utilities, with electricity and water being the most important. Therefore, the two companies proceeded to negotiate with the Chinese authorities, originally hoping that the extramural road issue could be resolved at an early date, but this did not materialize. Therefore, the electricity company feared that another company would obtain a concession in the area, which would result in significant losses. In order to protect itself, it signed a special contract with the Chinese authorities on January 4 this year to establish the West District Electricity Company to undertake the electricity supply. The signing of this contract has led to an extremely complex situation. The Board of Directors has taken steps to protect the Bureau's rights and interests, but for the long-term interests of the citizens, it prefers to consider practical cooperation rather than insist on a strict interpretation of legal texts.

Telephone Rate Increase Incident

In January of this year, the telephone company petitioned for a rate increase, hoping to reach 22.89% of total revenue. According to the franchise contract, the company is entitled to a one-point dividend, but the company claims that this cannot be achieved with the current rates. This has caused many protests, but the public seems to be largely unaware of the content of this issue. The franchise contract must be observed by both parties, and the company has the right to demand its fulfillment. Since the company has proven that its revenue has not reached the amount stipulated in the contract, the Bureau cannot but allow the rate increase according to the agreement. Otherwise, the Bureau would be in breach of contract and would be liable for damages. The current problem facing the Board of Directors is not whether a rate increase is appropriate during a time of economic depression, but whether the company has the right to increase rates. As for the actual amount of the increase, the Bureau has reviewed it and believes that an increase of up to 12.5% is sufficient to meet the needs (subject to the approval of the French Concession). As for the implementation of pay-per-call billing, this is another issue. In general, pay-per-call billing is indeed in line with economic principles, but there are various local conditions that must be carefully considered. This is something that the Bureau can decide.

Rickshaw Reform Proposal

In May of last year, the Bureau established a Rickshaw Affairs Committee to promote reform proposals. However, in order to avoid the forced unemployment of rickshaw pullers, drastic measures were not taken. The Bureau's main objective is to improve the living conditions of rickshaw pullers, but the necessary preparatory procedures must be carried out first, such as registering rickshaw owners, reducing rickshaw rentals, registering rickshaw pullers, and improving vehicles. The registration of public rickshaw pullers has been progressing rapidly since warnings were issued to rickshaw owners, and has now reached 18,000. It is expected to be completed by June of this year. Considering the many difficulties encountered by the Rickshaw Affairs Committee, it can be said that it has achieved considerable success.

Allocation of Education Funds

Due to financial constraints, the Board of Directors had to reconsider the original education plan last year. As a result, it was decided that: (1) the total amount of education funds should not exceed two percent of the municipal tax and its associated land tax; (2) the expenses of the Bureau's Chinese and foreign children's schools should be given priority, but efforts should be made to reduce costs; (3) except for those already provided for in the budget, the construction of new schools should be postponed; (4) the subsidies for Chinese private schools should be increased by 50,000 yuan, and the subsidies for Japanese schools should be increased by 20,000 yuan. Given the current financial situation, this will still have to be done this year. However, this year, the subsidies for Japanese schools are expected to increase from 118,000 yuan to 128,000 yuan, and the subsidies for Chinese schools are expected to increase from 188,500 yuan to 208,760 yuan.

Factory Inspection Incident

At the 1933 annual meeting, the previous Chairman believed that the integrity of administration within the concession should be maintained. However, the Chinese authorities believed that all Chinese and foreign factories within the concession should comply with factory laws. After two years, there is still no way to reconcile these two opposing views, and the amended Attached Rule No. 34 is still not convenient to implement. However, in the past year, the Bureau has made considerable progress in adjusting and improving the industrial environment. Systematic investigations have been carried out on factory building structures, cleaning equipment, fire risk prevention, and the use of dangerous goods.

Report on Revenue and Expenditure in the Past Year

The 1934 financial report shows that various economies have saved a total of 1.1 million yuan in regular expenses. However, at the same time, tax revenue has also decreased by 440,000 yuan, so the surplus is only 700,000 yuan. However, because 2 million yuan of reserve funds were used under the revenue item, the actual situation is still that expenditures exceed revenue. As for temporary expenses, due to the slow progress of construction projects, approximately 1 million yuan less was spent. Based on the motion of last year's annual meeting, 7 million yuan in public bonds were raised in May. For a time, the subscription was very prosperous, but by the end of the year, the amount of 5.5 million yuan was still short. This must be included in this year's adjustment, etc. After the Chairman's report, it was passed by the whole body.

Current Year's Budget

Next, the fifth item on the agenda was discussed, and the Chairman presented the budget proposal for the current year and requested its approval. Chairman Arnold said that the total regular income for this year, including the surplus from the previous year, is approximately 25,913,850 yuan, an increase of approximately 850,000 yuan over the previous year. Among them, municipal taxes, license fees, and public utility revenue are all expected to increase. Of the income, 2,270,510 yuan should be allocated to education expenses. Regular expenses, excluding education expenses, are estimated to be 24,807,530 yuan (24,126,590 yuan last year). Now, all departments are making every effort to tighten expenditures, and new projects will not be undertaken unless they are urgently needed. However, given the size of this concession, municipal services must maintain their efficiency even during times of economic depression. In addition, in 1934, it was announced that the first batch of principal repayment funds had been allocated from this year onwards. This is done in accordance with past precedents. The total regular budget deficit is approximately 1.2 million yuan. According to normal theory, taxes should be increased to compensate for this. After careful consideration, it is still proposed to allocate from the reserve fund. However, the reserve fund will eventually be exhausted, so after the market improves, it must be considered to restore the previous tax rates to avoid hindering the rational development of municipal facilities. In the temporary budget, construction costs have been reduced significantly compared to last year. Those that have been stipulated are almost all limited to completing the work that has already been started and the road projects that can no longer be delayed. As for the new buildings in the police and health departments, they will not be started until the economic situation improves. A total of 14 million yuan has been listed under the item of debt repayment. It is hoped that it will be possible to raise debts within the year so that this can be carried out. Under the item of temporary income, it is planned to withdraw 8 million yuan from the debt repayment fund to repay the 19)5 public bonds, which is also part of the aforementioned 14 million. In addition, it is planned to sell some surplus land. The amount that is not enough should be requested from the taxpayers to authorize the Board of Directors to raise debts as appropriate, up to a maximum of 15.5 million yuan, etc. It was passed by the whole body.

Orchestra Case

After the election of candidates for the sixth and seventh items on the agenda (see above), the eighth item, Mr. Hausenrob's motion to transfer the orchestra to a private organization with an annual subsidy of 150,000 yuan, was discussed. First, Chairman Arnold said that at last year's annual meeting, the previous Chairman proposed to abolish the orchestra for financial reasons, but this was not passed. Now, the Board of Directors still maintains its historical attitude and leaves the decision on the existence or abolition of the orchestra to the taxpayers. The history of the orchestra dates back to before 1881, when it was originally organized by a private organization. Later, due to insufficient funding, it was decided by the taxpayers' meeting in that year that the Board of Directors would take over. However, it seems that the proposer of this motion did not consult with the relevant people beforehand, and the proposed method is extremely impractical. It is obviously a regressive action. What the taxpayers should decide today is only the word "existence" or "abolition," etc. The Chairman then put it to a vote, and as a result, Mr. Hausenrob's motion was rejected.

Proposal to Levy Taxes

Then, the ninth item on the agenda, Mr. Hausenrob's motion to investigate the possibility of levying taxes on vacant houses, vacant land, and unregistered land, and to publish the results, was discussed. The Chairman rose and said that the proposer of this motion seemed unaware that the Board of Directors had conducted detailed research on this issue for many years. In 1870, the taxpayers' annual meeting resolved that the Board of Directors should levy taxes on all unregistered land, regardless of the nationality of the landowner. In the following three years' budget proposals, this item of income was listed. However, in reality, the Bureau only received 18 taels, 9 mace, and 4 fen. This is because the holders of unregistered land are in possession of Chinese land deeds, and the Bureau cannot order them to present them for inspection. Since there is no way to know who the landowner is, or the relationship between the four boundaries, area, transfer, and division, it is impossible to levy taxes unless the landowner is willing to declare it for his own benefit. Since then, until 1893, this issue was raised again due to the demarcation of Hongkou. In 1920, due to the end of the European War, some people argued that since the registration of the Austrian consulate had been cancelled, the land that had been registered under it had become unregistered land and could not be subject to land tax. This proposal was rejected by the Board of Directors, as the Bureau had never given up the right to levy taxes on unregistered land, even if it could not collect taxes. From 1920 to the present, this issue has been raised due to various events. The Board of Directors has done its best to investigate, but because it involves political, legal, and practical aspects, if a survey report is rashly published, it will only affect the possibility of its resolution. Now, the difficulty of this issue is gradually being resolved, and the Board of Directors is studying further methods. For the benefit of taxpayers and the public, it is best to allow the Board of Directors to act expediently and not be constrained by frivolous opinions. Therefore, although the proposer of this motion is full of public spirit, from the overall point of view, it is still hoped that the attendees will reject it. What has been said above is only a discussion of the levying of taxes on unregistered land, but the situation for levying taxes on vacant houses with no occupants is exactly the same. Moreover, the levying of taxes on unregistered land has long been implemented, and it seems that the proposer did not know this, etc. The Chairman then put it to a vote, and as a result, this motion was also rejected.

Purchase of Land to Widen Roads

Discussing the tenth item on the agenda, Mr. Hausenrob proposed to raise 5 million yuan to purchase land and expand roads. The Chairman rose again and said that this motion is entirely a financial issue. The Board of Directors' policy has always been to take the opportunity to acquire land and widen roads whenever houses are rebuilt, as this can save costs and reduce interference with the commercial activities of the area. If land acquisition can be carried out promptly, it will naturally be in the public interest. From 1929 to 1933, the Bureau's expenditure on this item was approximately 1.5 million taels per year. Last year, it was also above 1.5 million yuan. Including road repair costs, nearly 14 million yuan has been spent in the past five years. However, in view of the current situation, construction costs must be drastically reduced in order to overcome this difficulty. In the temporary budget for this year, the Board of Directors has requested permission to raise 15.5 million yuan, which includes the cost of expanding roads. However, given the current economic situation, it is almost impossible to raise public debts. Moreover, if the proposed 5 million yuan can be raised, the construction costs after the land acquisition will require an additional 350,000 yuan per year. If taxes are not increased, other projects will inevitably be put on hold and funds will be diverted to this use. Therefore, as far as the current situation is concerned, there is no need to adopt this motion. If increasing the amount of debt is indeed beneficial, the Board of Directors will automatically make this request, etc. As a result, this motion was also rejected.

Telephone Rate Increase

Finally, the eleventh item, Mr. Kanematsu's motion to request the Board of Directors to negotiate with the telephone company to postpone the rate increase, was discussed. At this point, the atmosphere at the meeting suddenly became tense. First, Mr. Kanematsu, the Secretary-General of the Japanese Youth Association and the original proposer, took the stage to give a speech, eloquently explaining the reasons for the proposal and explaining and refuting the pre-drawn large telephone company rate increase chart in detail. He said that this was not a matter for a part of the Japanese residents, but was related to the interests of all Shanghai citizens. The telephone company belongs to Shanghai and should serve all of Shanghai, etc. This won warm applause from the entire venue. His speech briefly stated that, according to past official reports, there have been four telephone company rate increases. The first time, the company authorities requested an increase of 40%. The second time, the Board of Directors advocated an increase of 25%. The third time, the company requested an increase of 22%. The fourth time, the Board of Directors advocated an increase of 12.5%. In addition, there have been several informal increase reports. At a time when the economy is declining and all industries are sluggish, this rate increase is deeply difficult for people of all countries and all sectors of society. Calculating on the basis of the telephone company's capital of 135 million yuan, if the rates are increased according to the new regulations, it will be 2% in the first year, 15% in the seventh year, 20% in the ninth year, and 25% in the eleventh year. Rather than causing future disputes, it is better to resolve them as soon as possible. Moreover, since the Board of Directors has reduced the promised 11.5% to 10%, eliminating the rate increase is not absolutely impossible, etc. Then, the Chairman rose again and said that he had mentioned in his annual report that the telephone company has the right to increase rates in accordance with the franchise contract. The public must know that the franchise contract creates significant obligations and responsibilities and cannot be unilaterally abolished. In order to fulfill its obligations, the Board of Directors has allowed it to increase rates by no more than 12.5%. However, how to increase them has not yet been determined. Now, it cannot break its promise. Moreover, any resolution of the taxpayers cannot abolish or change its contract without the consent of the company. If a dispute arises due to the resolution of the annual meeting, the company can request a ruling in accordance with the contract, and the result of the ruling will inevitably uphold the company's rights and allow a rate increase that far exceeds 12.5%. At the same time, the Bureau will have to pay a huge amount of damages. As for the statement that the rate increase should be determined after expert investigation, in 1929, the Bureau had already spent a large sum of money to hire internationally renowned experts to investigate this matter. Their report advocated a rate increase of 35%. Later, they even said that if they had foreseen the changes in exchange rates at that time, they would have advocated an even greater increase. However, after negotiations between the Board of Directors and the company, the rates were only increased three years later after the completion of the automatic switching equipment (March 1932) according to the experts' recommendations. The company also agreed not to seek any further increases for the next two years. As far as the current situation is concerned, there is no need to spend a large sum of money to re-invite experts. Moreover, it seems unlikely that experts will deny the rate increase in order to maintain the contract. As for the current matter, it is only a financial issue, and the Bureau's staff is fully capable of handling it. In short, if the taxpayers' meeting makes a hasty decision, the result may be that the taxpayers will be placed in an unfavorable position, and it will not be possible to abolish the contract in the end. It is hoped that the attendees will deal with it carefully, etc.

Organize a Special Committee

After a debate on this motion that lasted for an hour, the Chairman put it to a vote. As a result, it was passed with amendments to Mr. Kanematsu's original proposal, that is, adding the organization of a special committee to investigate, research, and handle it to the eleventh original proposal. For the sake of prudence, the Chairman held a further vote when adjourning the meeting and leaving the venue. As a result, it was passed by 371 votes to 263 votes against. The adjournment was then announced. It was already 8:00 PM.

Articles of Association of the Executive Committee

Articles of Association of the Executive Committee of the Civilian Welfare Undertaking Management Committee: (1) These Articles of Association are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 4 of the Regulations of the Civilian Welfare Undertaking Management Committee; (2) This Executive Committee is organized by a number of members designated by the Mayor. The Secretary-General of the Municipal Government is the Chairman of this Executive Committee, and the Secretary-General of the Management Committee is the Recording Secretary of this Executive Committee; (3) The powers and responsibilities of this Executive Committee are as follows: 1. To prepare and review all budgets, final accounts, and financial reports for submission to the Management Committee; 2. To review the various plans of the subcommittees and the Secretariat; 3. To handle the various affairs entrusted by the Management Committee; 4. To request the Chairman of the Management Committee to appoint and dismiss assistant secretaries and other staff; 5. To compile various undertaking work reports and submit them to the Management Committee for review; (4) This Executive Committee is temporarily scheduled to hold a regular meeting once a month, and extraordinary meetings may be convened by the Chairman when necessary. A certain number of members of this Committee constitutes a quorum for attendance; (5) These Articles of Association may be amended by the Management Committee.

Organization of the Secretariat of the Management Committee

Attached: Organization of the Secretariat of the Management Committee and Detailed Rules of Procedure: (1) This Committee shall appoint a Secretary-General appointed by the Mayor, who shall manage all affairs within the Committee on behalf of this Committee; (2) Under the Secretary-General, there may be a number of Assistant Secretaries to assist in all affairs; (3) The duties of the Secretariat are as follows: 1. Documents and publicity; 2. Accounting; 3. General affairs; 4. Research, design, and construction; 5. Social education undertakings; 6. Training staff; 7. Rickshaw management; (4) The organization and detailed rules of this department may be amended by the Management Committee.

Record of Mayor Wu's Opening Speech

Ladies and gentlemen, today, the Shanghai Municipal Government's Civilian Welfare Undertaking Management Committee is holding its inaugural meeting. I am very grateful for the enthusiastic support of all the members and for taking the time to attend. At the same time, I am even more pleased that the civilian welfare undertakings of this city, thanks to the enthusiastic support of the leaders of all sectors of this city, have been transformed from ideals and hopes into facts and have begun to be implemented. Today, I would like to take this opportunity to report to you the purpose of this city in undertaking civilian welfare undertakings and ask for your guidance. Following the social and economic changes after the Industrial Revolution, the duties of modern governments have become increasingly complex due to the needs of the objective era. The meaning of modern countries, whether left-leaning or right-leaning, has shifted from passive securityism to active socialism. Matters that governments did not pay attention to or even interfere with in the past have now become the obligations that governments should fulfill, and these obligations have been stipulated in the constitutions of various countries after the European War. Although the current stage of China's social economy has not yet reached the stage of industrial development, and the revolutionary strategy of Marxism has been proven to be absolutely unsuitable for China by objective social conditions, we observe from a historical perspective that China's political philosophy has its own characteristics that are different from those of other countries, that is, the moderate Confucianism, whose ideal of nation-building also deeply contains the spirit of socialism, such as the so-called "men have their duties, women have their homes, the strong are employed, the young are nurtured, and the widowed, orphaned, lonely, disabled, and sick are all cared for." Therefore, the governance of ancient China has always been based on education and care as the two major principles. From a realistic perspective, our revolutionary mentor, Mr. Sun Yat-sen, said in his instructions on the steps of nation-building, "The primary task of construction is people's livelihood." At the same time, he said more specifically in the law on the implementation of local autonomy, "Local autonomous organizations are not only political organizations, but also economic organizations. In recent years, the duties of governments in civilized countries have gradually expanded from politics to economics. In ancient China, governance combined education and care. Later generations regressed, and the government abandoned the duties of education and care and allowed the people to care for and educate themselves. The government only existed as a passive entity that did not disturb the people, which was considered good governance. By the Han and Tang dynasties, the responsibility of protecting and governing the people had not yet been abandoned, so they were still able to resist strong enemies externally and redress grievances internally. Later, even this was abandoned, and the country was destroyed and the government ceased to exist. Civilization was lost, and the barbarians enjoyed the benefits of this for more than three hundred years. The people of the Republic of China should quickly establish the foundation of a thousand-year-old Republic of China with local autonomy. It is appropriate to learn from the trend of the world, adopt the latest ideals, and seek the happiness of all the people. Therefore, the responsibility of Chinese statesmen at this time should be to meet the trend of the times, take the spirit of catching up, and build a new society and a new country for the benefit of all the people, in order to establish a foundation for a thousand-year-old Republic of China. Because the resolution of the problems of the majority of civilians is not only a direct benefit to the civilians themselves, but also the starting point of the country and society. Although the past few years in this city have been a time of hardship and difficulty, it is now gradually showing signs of recovery. From now on, we should naturally seek active construction. In order to implement this goal, we have specifically designated this year as the Year of Social Construction and have given special attention to the implementation of civilian welfare undertakings. I have already reported on these undertakings and announced them in various newspapers, and I think you have all seen them. However, in order to promote their implementation, how to proceed smoothly, and achieve satisfactory results, we must hope for the practical guidance, mutual cooperation, and enthusiastic support of all of you.

Reading the Vow to Use National Goods

Mayor Wu and others were elected as the Presidium

Educational News

Ministry of Education Order: Setting up Training Classes for Private School Teachers

Using Summer Vacation for Training (Nanjing, 17th)

The Ministry of Education has ordered all departments and bureaus, stating: "Upon investigation, the organization and curriculum of private schools mostly do not comply with the regulations of educational laws. Most of their teachers are also unqualified elementary school teachers, often being completely unaware of teaching and training methods. While these should be strictly prohibited, considering the current state of education not yet being widespread, their existence can be permitted within the scope that does not hinder local elementary school enrollment. Educational administrative organs should make every effort to supervise and guide them to improve, thereby assisting in the promotion of compulsory education.

Now, to improve private schools and promote compulsory education, you are hereby instructed to inform your subordinates. Educational administrative organs in all counties and cities should, starting from this year, make use of summer vacation to gather private school teachers from various places and organize training classes for them. The subjects should be based on the actual needs of the teachers, focusing on basic knowledge and teaching methods in subjects such as Mandarin, arithmetic, and general knowledge. The lectures should emphasize the explanation of practical problems and practical exercises, rather than lecturing on theoretical knowledge. Examinations should be conducted afterward as a basis for rewards and punishments. The specific measures for the training classes should be promptly drafted in detail according to local conditions and submitted to the Ministry for review before the end of May."

Ministry of Education Report: Equipment for Science, Chemistry, and Biology in Secondary Schools (Nanjing, 17th)

The Ministry of Education has ordered all departments and bureaus, stating: "It is essential for secondary schools to have complete equipment for physics, chemistry, and biology (zoology and botany in junior high) to enhance teaching effectiveness. The Ministry has previously established standards for equipment in these subjects in secondary schools and has ordered compliance. Currently, the Ministry needs to assess whether the equipment in secondary schools in various provinces and cities is adequate. Please promptly investigate and list the equipment status of each subject in public and private secondary schools under your jurisdiction and formulate future improvement plans, submitting them for review within one month of receiving this document."

Liu Fu's Bereavement Funds of 12,000 Distributed (Nanjing, 17th)

The bereavement funds of 12,000 yuan for the late professor Liu Fu of Peking University were remitted by the Ministry of Finance to Peking University today. After verification, they will be transferred to Liu's surviving family members as soon as possible.

Hu Shuhua Takes Office as President of Chongqing University (Chongqing, 17th)

Hu Shuhua, the president of Chongqing University, has arrived in Chongqing from Hunan to assume his duties.

The Ministries of Industry and Education Will Promote Labor Education Experimental Zones

Regarding the promotion of labor education, the Ministries of Industry and Education have organized a design committee to plan and implement it. Last year, the two ministries sent personnel to Shanghai and Wuxi to provide guidance. Labor education experimental zones have been established in both Shanghai and Wuxi to promote labor education. The steering committees of the experimental zones in both locations have submitted reports to the two ministries on the implementation of labor education experiments. It is reported that the Ministries of Industry and Education are now planning the second phase, which involves promoting labor education in Hankou, Qingdao, and Tianjin. The two ministries plan to instruct the local authorities in each city to first report on the current status of labor education facilities in their respective areas and then guide them in establishing experimental zones and implementing measures.

Ministry of Education Urges Compilation of Simplified Character List

On the 16th, the Ministry of Education sent a letter to Li Shaoxi and Wang Yian, urging them to complete the compilation of the first phase of the simplified character list and submit it to the Ministry for review as soon as possible to facilitate its early implementation.

Opening of Zhejiang Provincial Local Education Guidance Conference

Over 50 Attendees, Director Xu Chairs

Academic Presentations in the Morning, Group Discussions in the Afternoon

The sixth session of the Zhejiang Provincial Local Education Guidance Conference opened at 8:00 AM yesterday in the Education Department auditorium. More than 50 representatives attended. Director of Education Xu Shaodi presided over the meeting, leading the attendees in a ceremony and delivering a report. Subsequently, Luo Dixian, Zhao Jiyu, Zhang Rentian, Jin Haiguan, Lin Ben, and Xu Xudong gave speeches. Group discussions on proposals began at 1:00 PM. The details are as follows:

Chairman's Report

Chairman Xu, the Director of Education, reported, stating briefly that the Zhejiang school guidance system has achieved considerable success, which needs to be continued with efforts in the future. There are also many aspects that need to be improved. He listed six points for attention. Subsequently, as Director Xu had to attend a meeting at the Provincial Government, Secretary Lin Qi served as his proxy.

Academic Presentations

First, Section Chief Luo gave a presentation, stating briefly that the Ministry of Education has ordered the establishment of elementary school research associations in various places. The implementation of school district guidance areas in the province has yielded good results. We should request the Ministry of Education to adopt flexible measures and simultaneously compile and print guidance activity reports for other places to learn from. He also discussed the establishment of sections in the bureau, believing that such facilities should focus on the human aspect rather than the system. Regarding education funding, we have made every effort to tighten our belts and have secured one million yuan. Next, Section Chief Zhao gave a presentation, stating briefly that education should focus on rural areas and utilize other forces to cooperate in its implementation. He also explained the points for attention listed by Director Xu, item by item. Subsequently, Zhang Rentian, the magistrate of Xindeng County, Lin Sheng, the principal of a people's education school, Xu Xudong of Hangzhou Normal School, and Jin Haiguan, the principal of a rural normal school, each gave speeches.

Group Discussions

After the speeches, the meeting was temporarily adjourned. All attendees had lunch at the Education Department. Group discussions began at 1:00 PM. Zhao Ganyu presided over the social education group, and Jin Zuxian presided over the elementary education group. (The above were held separately in the Education Department auditorium.) Literacy Education Committee

Branch Offices to Be Established in Each District Next Month

Teachers for Literacy Schools Must Pass Examination and Training

Propaganda Conference to Be Held Tomorrow to Discuss Expanding Propaganda

The preparatory work of the Literacy Education Committee of this city is currently quite intense. In addition to the Jiangwan and Hunan Experimental Zones, which were established earlier, the branch offices in each district will be established uniformly on May 1st. From May 8th, a survey of out-of-school citizens will begin. Teachers for literacy schools must pass an examination and be trained in training classes organized by the committee before being assigned to various schools. The committee has also scheduled a propaganda conference at the Municipal Party Headquarters at 2:00 PM tomorrow to discuss expanding propaganda. The teacher examination methods and organizational rules for district offices drafted by the committee are excerpted below:

Teacher Examination Methods

Shanghai Literacy Education Committee Literacy School Teacher Examination Methods, Article 1: The Shanghai Literacy Education Committee (hereinafter referred to as "this Committee") is holding an examination for teachers of the Literacy Schools of this Committee to select qualified teachers. Anyone willing to serve as a teacher in the Literacy Schools of this Committee should take the examination in accordance with these methods. Article 2: Anyone who has graduated from a junior high school or above, or has equivalent academic ability and has served as a teacher in an elementary school, secondary school, or people's school for more than one year, is between 20 and 40 years old, and can speak Mandarin and the Shanghai dialect may apply to take the examination. Article 3: Applicants should apply to this Committee, fill out the examination form, and submit supporting documents and two recent half-length photos. Article 4: The examination is divided into three parts: physical examination, written examination, and oral examination. (1) Physical examination: Those with a proper appearance, sound body, no bad habits, and no other infectious diseases, and who can endure hardship, are considered qualified. (2) Written examination subjects: (A) Mandarin; (B) General knowledge (including Party principles, society, nature, arithmetic, and phonetic symbols). (3) Oral examination: (A) Written examination subjects; (B) Language; (C) Habit examination. Article 5: Those who are admitted must undergo three to four weeks of training. The specific methods will be determined separately. Article 6: Those who are admitted and pass the examination after the training period will be issued a certificate by this Committee. Article 7: If, during the training or service period, there is improper conduct, ineffective teaching, or failure to follow the guidance and supervision of this Committee, this Committee will terminate the training or revoke their position. Article 8: The application and examination dates, locations, and the names of those admitted will be announced by this Committee in the newspaper. Article 9: These methods may be amended at any time if there are any matters not covered. Article 10: These methods will be implemented from the date of promulgation and reported to the Municipal Government for record.

Organization of District Offices

Shanghai Literacy Education Committee (hereinafter referred to as "this Committee") has divided this city into 22 districts for the convenience of implementing literacy education in this city, including 1 district in Hunan, 2 districts in Hunan, 3 districts in Hunan, 4 districts in Hunan, 1 district in Zhabei, 2 districts in Zhabei, 3 districts in Zhabei, Fahua District, Yangsi District, Tangqiao District, Caojing District, Lihang District, Gaohang District, Yihang District, Jiangwan District, Pengpu District, Gaoqiao District, Zhenru District, Pusong District, Wusong District, Yangjing District, and Yinxiang District. These rules are hereby established. Article 2: Each district will have an office with a director and three sections: general affairs, guidance, and investigation. Each section will have a section chief and several staff members. Article 3: Each district office may, with the approval of this Committee, establish the following committees: (1) Investigation Committee; (2) Propaganda Committee; (3) Academic Affairs Committee. The members of the aforementioned committees will be selected by the district office from the district party headquarters, municipal committee members, school principals, public security bureau branch chiefs, and local citizens and appointed by this Committee. Each of the aforementioned committees will have a chairman designated by this Committee. Article 4: All staff members of the district office are unpaid and must diligently carry out their duties in accordance with the prescribed time. However, in special circumstances, this Committee may approve a modest allowance for expenses. Article 5: The duties of the district office are as follows: (1) To discuss and formulate plans for promoting literacy education in the district and submit them to the Municipal Literacy Education Committee for deliberation and implementation. (2) To discuss the establishment of literacy schools based on the number of out-of-school adults and children in the district. (3) To supervise and guide literacy schools in the district. (4) To liaise with various people's schools and religious organizations in the district to promote literacy education. (5) To review matters related to enrollment, exemption, and tutoring of out-of-school persons in the district. (6) To discuss and formulate methods for compelling enrollment in the district and punishing those who fail to enroll by the deadline or are absent from class without reason. (7) To handle examinations for out-of-school supplementary education for various people in the district. (8) To deliberate on other important matters related to literacy education in the district.

Matters to Be Handled by Each Section

Article 6: The director of each district office will, under the direction of this Committee, supervise the staff in handling all affairs and report their work achievements to this Committee. Article 7: The chief of the general affairs section will, under the direction of the director, be responsible for the following matters: (1) Handling documents, accounting, and general affairs. (2) Handling liaison and communication matters. (3) Handling matters not belonging to other sections. Article 8: The chief of the investigation section will, under the direction of the director, be responsible for the following matters: (1) Investigating out-of-school adults and children in the district and supervising their enrollment. (2) Investigating religious organizations in the district. (3) Investigating requests for deferment or exemption from school, out-of-school tutoring, and failure to enroll or absenteeism of out-of-school adults and children in the district. (4) Handling various statistical matters. (5) Regarding other investigation matters. Article 9: The chief of the guidance section will, under the direction of the director, be responsible for the following matters: (1) Guiding the equipment and training of literacy schools in the district. (2) Guiding the teaching of religious organizations in the district. (3) Assessing plans for improving literacy schools in the district. (5) Handling performance examinations for out-of-school supplementary education for various people in the district. (6) Regarding other guidance matters. Article 10: The director of each district office may convene office meetings for the convenience of managing office affairs. Article 11: These rules will be implemented after being approved by this Committee and reported to the Municipal Government for record.

Zhang Yuanruo Speaks on How to Study Legal Science

Yesterday was the ninth day of the National Reading Movement Conference organized by the Chinese Cultural Construction Association. Zhang Yuanruo, the director of the Shanghai College of Political Science and Law, was specially invited to speak on how to study legal science. The following is a transcript of his speech:

The Importance and Difficulty of Methods

Ladies and gentlemen, I am honored to be invited by the Chinese Cultural Construction Association to speak on how to study legal science. Due to time constraints, I cannot elaborate fully but can only provide a brief outline for your reference. First, we must understand the importance and difficulty of methods in studying legal science. The importance of methods can be explained in three points. First, the definition and nature of law are interpreted differently by various schools of thought. Scholars studying law often find it difficult to answer the question of the definition and nature of law. Therefore, those who are new to the study of law must seriously consider the method. Second, the various theories in legal science are vast and complex. How we can study their merits and demerits also depends on whether the method is appropriate. Third, the purpose of law is not to create rigid provisions but to apply them to govern people and maintain society. Therefore, law has a great impact on the prosperity and decline of a nation and the strength and weakness of a country. Therefore, the method of studying legal science must be considered. The importance of studying legal methods is as mentioned above, and the difficulty of studying methods cannot be fully explained in a few words. Now, I will explain it in three points. First, studying law is not only a scientific problem but also a philosophical problem. Therefore, beginners who want to make achievements in legal research must integrate and understand the various schools of thought to gain profound insights. Otherwise, they will not be able to use them freely. Second, from the static aspect of law, that is, from the theoretical aspect, it can be divided into philosophical, comparative, analytical, and social historical aspects. The various schools of thought are quite inconsistent, and each has its own strengths and weaknesses. Therefore, we must study the merits and demerits of each school of thought. From this, we can see the difficulty of the method. Third, from the dynamic perspective of the trend of the times, the study of law was narrowly defined in the past, that is, speaking about the law in terms of the law, only studying the wording of the provisions. Today, it is broadly defined and requires a profound study of various social sciences. In the past, it was only a theoretical study. Today, we must take into account the facts and consult extensively to be complete and sound. In the past, it was only a study of provisions. Today, it has evolved from the study of provisions to the study of practical applications. The importance of methods is as such, and the difficulty of methods is also so. Therefore, beginners should study with an objective attitude and an open mind and never introduce subjective prejudices.

Speaking from the Position of Academic Research

World academia can be divided into natural sciences and social sciences. The goal of natural science is to govern and utilize nature. The goal of social science is to govern and improve society. Law is not only a part of the field of social science but also a crystallization of various social sciences. Those who study law must not only have basic knowledge of legal science but also have a profound understanding of various disciplines such as politics, economics, ethics, religion, philosophy, logic, history, society, psychology, and anthropology. With the cultivation and preparation of the above disciplines, legal research can be advanced. Therefore, in terms of essence, law is at the forefront of social sciences. In terms of application, law is a tool for governing society in a passive sense and also has the function of improving society and promoting society in an active sense. From this, we can see its academic status. Therefore, beginners should recognize the noble greatness of law on the one hand. At the same time, the attitude of research should be humble and start from the basics. We must not be too ambitious. We must build our foundation from the above disciplines before we can achieve anything.

Speaking from the Content of the Learning Method

Our method of studying law should be to study substantive law first and then procedural law. Substantive law is civil law and criminal law. Procedural law is litigation law. Substantive law is the main law, and procedural law is the auxiliary law. We should study the main law first and then the auxiliary law. Second, we should study the common law first and then the special law. The common law is the basic laws and regulations and important laws and regulations. Special law is a specific type of law based on the common law. After studying the common law, studying the special law can be easily solved. Third, we should study the general theory first and then the specific theory. The general theory is the general theory of law, the general theory of civil law, and criminal administrative law. The specific theory is the law of obligations, property rights, and kinship. After we study the general theory, we can study the specific theory in an orderly manner and find a hierarchy.

Speaking from the Schools of Learning

The schools of world law are different, each with its own methods and conclusions. Those belonging to the pure theory school can be divided into the pure philosophy school and the natural law school. These two schools believe that law is not due to creation. They focus on the basis of legal theory and explore the essence of law outside of human-made law. They criticize the ideal standard of real law and seek its so-called rational law and natural law that can be passed down for all ages and applicable to all countries. Those belonging to the empirical school can be divided into the analytical school, the comparative law school, the historical school, and the sociological school. The analytical school studies the developed legal system and regards the legislator as a conscious creator. The comparative law school believes that law is a product of geography and race. The historical school believes that law is an accumulation of the spirit of the nation. The sociological school is based on the theory of the advocate of positive philosophy, Comte, and studies law as a social phenomenon. The schools of thought have different theories. Beginners should seek a correct understanding of the nature of law and humbly explore the strengths, weaknesses, similarities, and differences of each school of thought before they can gain a deep foundation.

Speaking from the Practical Application

Law is not a rigid, subjective provision. It is an objective social product that should be reformed and improved according to social needs and the trend of the times. Therefore, we should study general principles from concrete facts. Theories are often too empty. Whether the theory can be applied to the facts is a highly questionable issue. Therefore, the American scholar Foard strongly opposes mechanical legal science. Second, we should study from the perspective of objective function. The subjective provisions should be studied objectively and analytically. Law is produced for society, not society is produced for the application of law. Therefore, we should not focus on the provisions of the law itself but on social interests. Legal researchers should have a major realization that they should not only seek the fairness of the law and the ideal of fairness but also seek the fairness of implementation and the fairness of execution.

Speaking from the Required Conditions

Those who study law should first have a wealth of knowledge. Various social sciences must have a profound foundation. Second, they must be rich in practical experience. As the saying goes, heaven, reason, state, and law are human feelings. It can be said that the philosophical concept of Chinese law also has a clear understanding of the world and familiarity with human feelings. The so-called worldly affairs and human feelings are the source of formulating and applying the law. US President Lincoln did not study law, but he made a great contribution to the law. This is due to practical experience. Third, they must have a pure and great personality. Although law is not morality, it is a tool to protect morality. Moreover, law is a tool to govern people. Law enforcers should be role models for the masses. Therefore, those who study law should have a sound personality and great and pure integrity.

Prospects for Chinese Legal Science

Chinese legal circles have fallen to a low point. One of the reasons is that the traditional psychology of the general public is that law is cruel, unkind, and strict. This influence is not very profound. The most painful thing is that in recent times, the trickery of lawyers has made people feel that legal researchers are all corrupt and unfaithful people. In fact, there have been great legal researchers in Chinese history in all dynasties. Guan Zhong, Zichan, Shang Yang, Han Fei, Wang Anshi, Zhang Juzheng, Huang Lizhou, and others from the Zhou and Qin dynasties were all brilliant scholars in Chinese legal history. Therefore, those who govern the law in China should learn from Guan Zhong's sentiments. Second, due to the aggravation of the morbid state of the times, it has fallen into a low point. If we want to restore the glory of the past, those who govern the law must recognize the position of legal science in academics and its profound relationship with the strength of the country and the nation.

The End.

Gold Mark-up Rises Four Yuan

Swap Market More Short Than Long by Half a Yuan

Although the Central Bank, China Bank, and Sassoon continued to exert pressure, the daily bank and other buyers were quite strong. Market sentiment had already improved, resulting in a firm outcome. The customs gold unit fell by seven li, and the standard price for the gold mark-up fell to 861.2 yuan, leading to a lower opening in the morning. After the opening, banks showed strong buying interest, and major players took advantage of the low prices to return, actually breaking through the 20-yuan mark. The Bank of China blocked with shillings, hindering the upward trend and causing it to fall back below 20 yuan. The HSBC's listed prices were revealed, with both British and American rates remaining unchanged. At this time, Hengxing was still advancing with multiple trades, but Sassoon, the Central Bank, and others continued to sell, and the foreign exchange market loosened, falling once.
